Niklas Lollo<//Name>
<date>1626046533312<//date>< rating>
3</rating>
<review>For everyone looking to do Open Water Diver, here are the prices:
~$225 for the course (includes the main scuba rental items)
~$180 for the PADI e-learning (cannot be shared with anyone else)
~$50 for the guidebook, dive log, etc.
And you need to have fins (~$100), snorkel (~$40), mask (~$50), booties (~$50), and gloves (~$30), which can be rented ($40 per day?) or purchased (prices above).
Total is roughly $750.
Would be nice if this were quoted on the site.

Another thing you aren't made aware of on the course sign-up: you will have to drop off/pick up your air tanks from the store. You borrow two at a time and need one tank for every dive. This meant that for a course I took, I needed to visit the store 5 times for pick up/drop off of air/equipment. (We had four pool dives, 4 ocean dives. And actually we had to go an extra time, but that was unexpected.) A lot of extra driving and time I wasn't expecting, when the course is already quite demanding!

All the pool dives were completed within 2 or 3 hours, never 4 as quoted. We rarely went below 2000 psi on our tanks (though ymmv). Felt like those skill learnings could've been condensed into 2 or 3 days.

The orientation was OK, but felt more like a sales event for the "snorkeling" gear. I definitely felt pressured to buy and the orientation part did not feel meaningful--could have been accomplished online or on the night of the first pool dive.

The people in the rental department were pretty cool - I liked their calendar with random "holidays" - yoga day, rocky road day, etc.

Then there were the vagaries of the particular course I took, which I don't feel like getting into. Suffice to say, I'm getting my advanced cert at another shop in the area.

It wasn't the worst experience, but wasn't great either. I did get stoked to keep diving! But for how much money you're spending, it'd be nice to receive a consistently positive quality of service.< /review>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

Rod Jenkins< /user_name>
< time>
1438137263391< /time>
<rating>2< /rating><text>Definitely not your typical dive shop, and that is not a good thing. Being located within an office building should have tipped me off immediately but I proceeded to do business with them anyway because they are one of the very few PADI 5 Star IDC dive shops in San Diego. Upon entering you can tell this is a large organization and, as I continued to learn each time I visited over the past two years, has lost (or never had) the customer service touch within its bloated walls.

Staff is very hard to find - nary a greeting upon entrance. Sales staff, once identified and made aware you are an interested customer, provided good service. However looking for them becomes a chore that an organization with as many people on the payroll should not suffer.

On the service side, which is almost a completely different company within the Enterprise, seems out of touch with the meaning of customer relations. My most recent interaction with this staff resulted in a passive-aggressive attitude that is not required nor desired. The dive industry has for the most part eliminated the 'holy than thou' attitude, but it remains with these individuals. I tried attempting to correct this in person but unable to find a manager in a timely manner proved impossible (see previous paragraph).

Nothing negative to report on the rental side - that is a well run shop. But just like the service side, it is a completely separate 'company' internal to the Enterprise. What happens in one, stays there - it appeared there was no cross-talking between their systems.

Pricing: out of this world. Very large selection of items but each are priced very high. Items displayed as 'on sale' are marked down to the MSRP. Regulator service is also over-priced by a very large margin in what must be an attempt to make a nice profit. To maintain the Enterprise, one must charge the customers through the roof.

And finally, the little things that add up. Store opening on weekends is 0900 - how do you expect to service divers opening at such a late hour? Open at the latest by 0700. Social media marketing galore - but what supports these claims? Another 'business' focused on corporate sales - you can start to get the idea that the primary business model isn't focused on the individual customer.

I wanted to like this establishment but the Enterprise is just too big for itself. Have a look at how many instructors they have - 34 plus 13 assistant instructors/divemasters! I can't speak to how they excel on the instruction side but to maintain such a beast of an instructor pool doesn't come cheap.  Based on the high prices, the poor attitudes, and the lackluster service, I am no longer a patron of this dive shop.</text>< pics>
None</pics>

< Date>
1497018429268<//Date>
<Rating>4</Rating><Review>I thoroughly enjoyed the Teriyaki bowl from Golden Gate. It was a nice-sized piece of chicken breast that they chopped into slices and served over a bowl of fried rice. You may request white rice instead. I couldn't determine if lo mein could also be substituted. The rice wasn't all that, but the Teriyaki more than made up for it.

The space is small wit a couple of 4-seater booths and three or four 2-seater booths. It's set up buffet style with several of their most popular items in steam trays: fired rice, kung pao, sesame, beef /broccoli, egg rolls, shrimp. You may also order a la carte. For drinks they have a soda machine with coke products and they also have BANG! drinks which seem to be pretty popular in this area. Almost every QSR I've been too has them outside of the big chains.

A flat screen is situated over the seating area. You can't really watch it while you're dining. I think its for the staff.

The previous reviews are hit or miss which I attribute to new restaurant blues and growing pains. Again, its nothing to write home about, but if you're looking for decent Chinese fast food this is your place and it'll be mine for the forseeable future.</Review>< Pictures>

<text>I've been a car enthusiast since I was three years old.  The sales and service experience at a dealership matters to me, which is why my wife and I have purchased our last three 911s from Circle Porsche including a 2010 Turbo, 2015 Turbo S and 2018 GT3. The dealership is about 25 miles from our home and although there is a nearby Porsche dealer less than three miles away, traveling to Long Beach is a no-brainer for us.
At Circle Porsche, it's not just about selling vehicles.  General Manager, Eric Ernst, has a team of car enthusiasts who have a passion for motorsports.   We have always been treated fairly by a staff that has shared our excitement on each 911 purchase.  Also important is the fact that their deals are highly competitive.

Whether configuring a car for himself or for stock, Eric has ordered some truly exceptional cars and SUVs.  So a visit to the dealership to look at the inventory is always a cool experience.  Currently, there is a 911R on the showroom floor and later this year, Circle Porsche will take delivery of their first 911 GT2 RS.

If you're thinking about buying a new or used Porsche, I highly recommend Circle Porsche.  If you're considering a sports car, definitely drive a Porsche.  There are three "Rs" that really matter to me: Racing pedigree, Reputation, and Reliability.  All of these contribute to vehicles that are a blast to drive under all conditions and that represent Porsche's commitment to engineering and high performance.

Finally, Eric Ernst is part of the family that owns other dealerships in the area.  There aren't many family-owned dealerships anymore and a trip to Circle Porsche will make it apparent why the difference between their dealership and others owned by conglomerates is totally in the customer's best interests.

The itself theater is great and the food is good, especially for a movie theater/restaurant combination. I had a hamburger at my last visit that was served quickly and met my expectations, and I've never had a problem with service or with the food I've eaten there.
